<section class="ltx_appendix" id="A2">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_appendix" data-translate-id="chunk-255">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_appendix">Appendix B </span>Pre-training</h2>
<figure class="ltx_figure" id="A2.F9"><img alt="Refer to caption" class="ltx_graphics ltx_centering ltx_img_landscape" height="350" id="A2.F9.g1" src="x7.png" width="660">
<figcaption class="ltx_caption ltx_centering" data-translate-id="chunk-256"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_figure">Figure 9: </span>Learning curves comparing vision-to-text ratios (10:90, 20:80, 50:50) under fixed vision-text token budget across vision and language tasks. Early fusion with lower vision ratios tend to yield better results.</figcaption>
</figure>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="A2.SS1">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection" data-translate-id="chunk-257">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">B.1 </span>Joint-Training</h3>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A2.SS1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A2.SS1.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-258">We further provide the full training curves for all configurations in Figure&nbsp;<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#A2.F9" title="Figure 9 ‣ Appendix B Pre-training ‣ Kimi K2.5: Visual Agentic Intelligence"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">9</span></a>. Notably, we observe a "dip-and-recover" pattern in text performance during mid-fusion and late-fusion stages: when vision data is first introduced, text capability initially degrades before gradually recovering. We attribute this to the modality domain shift—the sudden introduction of vision tokens disrupts the established linguistic representation space, forcing the model to temporarily sacrifice text-specific competence for cross-modal alignment.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A2.SS1.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A2.SS1.p2.1" data-translate-id="chunk-259">In contrast, early fusion maintains a healthier and more stable text performance curve throughout training. By co-optimizing vision and language from the outset, the model naturally evolves unified multimodal representations without the shock of late-stage domain migration. This suggests that early exposure not only prevents the representation collapse observed in late fusion but also facilitates smoother gradient landscapes for both modalities. Collectively, these findings reinforce our proposal of native multimodal pre-training: moderate vision ratios combined with early fusion yield superior convergence properties and more robust bi-modal competence under fixed token budgets.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="A2.SS2">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection" data-translate-id="chunk-260">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">B.2 </span>Text data</h3>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A2.SS2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A2.SS2.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-261">The Kimi K2.5 pre-training text corpus comprises curated, high-quality data spanning four primary domains: Web Text, Code, Mathematics, and Knowledge. Most data processing pipelines follow the methodologies outlined in Kimi K2&nbsp;<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#bib.bib108" title="Kimi k2: open agentic intelligence">53</a>]</cite>. For each domain, we performed rigorous correctness and quality validation and designed targeted data experiments to ensure the curated dataset achieved both high diversity and effectiveness.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A2.SS2.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A2.SS2.p2.1" data-translate-id="chunk-262"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A2.SS2.p2.1.1">Enhanced Code Intelligence</span>
We upweighted code-centric data, significantly expanding (1) repository-level code supporting cross-file reasoning and architectural understanding, (2) issues, code reviews and commit histories from the internet capturing real-world development patterns, and (3) code-related documents retrieved from PDF and webtext corpora. These efforts strengthen repository-level comprehension for complex coding tasks, improve performance on agentic coding subtasks such as patch generation and unit test writing, and enhance code-related knowledge capabilities.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="A2.SS3">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection" data-translate-id="chunk-263">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">B.3 </span>Vision data</h3>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A2.SS3.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A2.SS3.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-264">Our multimodal pre-training corpus includes seven categories: caption, interleaving, OCR, knowledge, perception, video, and agent data. Caption data&nbsp;<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#bib.bib41" title="Laion-5b: an open large-scale dataset for training next generation image-text models">49</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#bib.bib42" title="Datacomp: in search of the next generation of multimodal datasets">18</a>]</cite> provides fundamental modality alignment, with strict limits on synthetic captions to mitigate hallucination. Image-text interleaving data from books, web pages, and tutorials&nbsp;<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#bib.bib43" title="Multimodal c4: an open, billion-scale corpus of images interleaved with text">81</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#bib.bib44" title="Obelics: an open web-scale filtered dataset of interleaved image-text documents">31</a>]</cite> enables multi-image comprehension and longer context learning. OCR data spans multilingual text, dense layouts, and multi-page documents. Knowledge data incorporates academic materials processed via layout parsers to develop visual reasoning capabilities.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A2.SS3.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A2.SS3.p2.1" data-translate-id="chunk-265">Furthermore, we curate a specialized multimodal problem-solving corpus to bolster reasoning within Science, Technology, Engineering, and Mathematics domains. This data is aggregated through targeted retrieval and web crawling; for informational content lacking explicit query formats, we employ in-context learning&nbsp;<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#bib.bib9" title="Language models are few-shot learners">10</a>]</cite> to automatically reformulate raw materials into structured academic problems spanning K-12 to university levels. To bridge the modality gap between visual layouts and code data, we incorporate extensive image-code paired data. This includes a diverse array of code formats—such as HTML, React, and SVG, among others—paired with their corresponding rendered screenshots, enabling the model to align abstract structural logic with concrete visual geometry.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A2.SS3.p3">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A2.SS3.p3.1" data-translate-id="chunk-266">For agentic and temporal understanding, we collect GUI screenshots and action trajectories across desktop, mobile, and web environments, including human-annotated demonstrations. Video data from diverse sources enables both hour-long video comprehension and fine-grained spatio-temporal perception. Additionally, we incorporate grounding data to enhance fine-grained visual localization, including perception annotations (bounding boxes), point-based references. We also introduce a new contour-level segmentation task&nbsp;<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#bib.bib16" title="Towards pixel-level vlm perception via simple points prediction">51</a>]</cite> for pixel-level perception learning. All data undergoes rigorous filtering, deduplication, and quality control to ensure high diversity and effectiveness.</p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section class="ltx_appendix" id="A3">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_appendix" data-translate-id="chunk-267">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_appendix">Appendix C </span>Infra</h2>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A3.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A3.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-268">Kimi K2.5 is trained on NVIDIA H800 GPU clusters with 8<math alttext="\times" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A3.p1.1.m1" intent=":literal"><semantics><mo>×</mo><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\times</annotation></semantics></math>400 Gbps RoCE interconnects across nodes. We employ a flexible parallelism strategy combining 16-way Pipeline Parallelism (PP) with virtual stages&nbsp;<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#bib.bib10" title="GPipe: efficient training of giant neural networks using pipeline parallelism">26</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#bib.bib11" title="Efficient large-scale language model training on gpu clusters using megatron-lm">39</a>]</cite>, 16-way Expert Parallelism (EP)&nbsp;<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#bib.bib12" title="Gshard: scaling giant models with conditional computation and automatic sharding">32</a>]</cite>, and ZeRO-1 Data Parallelism, enabling training on any number of nodes that is a multiple of 32. EP all-to-all communication is overlapped with computation under interleaved 1F1B scheduling. To fit activations within GPU memory constraints, we apply selective recomputation for <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="A3.p1.1.1">LayerNorm</span>, <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="A3.p1.1.2">SwiGLU</span>, and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="A3.p1.1.3">MLA</span> up-projections, compress insensitive activations to FP8-E4M3, and offload remaining activations to CPU with overlapped streaming.</p>
</div>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="A3.SS1">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection" data-translate-id="chunk-269">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">C.1 </span>Data Storage and Loading</h3>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A3.SS1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A3.SS1.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-270">We employ S3 <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#bib.bib15" title="Amazon simple storage service (amazon s3)">3</a>]</cite> compatible object storage solutions from cloud providers to house our VLM datasets.
To bridge the gap between data preparation and model training, we retain visual data in its native format and have engineered a highly efficient and adaptable data loading infrastructure.
This infrastructure offers several critical advantages:</p>
<ul class="ltx_itemize" id="A3.I1">
<li class="ltx_item" id="A3.I1.i1" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A3.I1.i1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A3.I1.i1.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-271"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A3.I1.i1.p1.1.1">Flexibility:</span> Facilitates dynamic data shuffling, blending, tokenization, loss masking, and sequence packing throughout the training process, enabling adjustable data ratios as requirements evolve;</p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="A3.I1.i2" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A3.I1.i2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A3.I1.i2.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-272"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A3.I1.i2.p1.1.1">Augmentation:</span> Allows for stochastic augmentation of both visual and textual modalities, while maintaining the integrity of 2D spatial coordinates and orientation metadata during geometric transformations;</p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="A3.I1.i3" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A3.I1.i3.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A3.I1.i3.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-273"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A3.I1.i3.p1.1.1">Determinism:</span> Guarantees fully deterministic training through meticulous management of random seeds and worker states, ensuring that any training interruption can be resumed seamlessly — the data sequence after resumption remains identical to an uninterrupted run;</p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="A3.I1.i4" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A3.I1.i4.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A3.I1.i4.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-274"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A3.I1.i4.p1.1.1">Scalability:</span> Achieves superior data loading throughput via tiered caching mechanisms, robustly scaling to large distributed clusters while regulating request frequency to object storage within acceptable bounds.</p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
<p class="ltx_p" id="A3.SS1.p1.2" data-translate-id="chunk-275">Furthermore, to uphold uniform dataset quality standards, we have built a unified platform overseeing data registration, visualization, statistical analysis, cross-cloud synchronization, and lifecycle governance.</p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section class="ltx_appendix" id="A4">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_appendix" data-translate-id="chunk-276">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_appendix">Appendix D </span>Unified Agentic Reinforcement Learning Environment</h2>
<figure class="ltx_figure" id="A4.F10"><img alt="Refer to caption" class="ltx_graphics ltx_centering ltx_img_landscape" height="268" id="A4.F10.g1" src="x8.png" width="664">
<figcaption class="ltx_caption ltx_centering" data-translate-id="chunk-277"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_figure">Figure 10: </span>Overview of our agentic RL framework.</figcaption>
</figure>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A4.SS0.SSS0.Px1">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-278">Environment</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A4.SS0.SSS0.Px1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A4.SS0.SSS0.Px1.p1.2" data-translate-id="chunk-279">To support unified Agentic RL, our RL framework features a standardized Gym-like <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#bib.bib195" title="OpenAI gym">9</a>]</cite> interface to streamline the implementation of diverse environments. Such design empowers users to implement and customize environments with minimal overhead. Our design prioritizes compositional modularity by integrating a suite of pluggable components, such as a <span class="ltx_text ltx_markedasmath ltx_font_italic" id="A4.SS0.SSS0.Px1.p1.2.1">Toolset</span> module for supporting various tools with sandboxes, a <span class="ltx_text ltx_markedasmath ltx_font_italic" id="A4.SS0.SSS0.Px1.p1.2.2">Judge</span> module for multi-faceted reward signals, and specialized modules for prompt diversification and instruction-following enhancement. These components can be dynamically composed with core agent loops, offering high flexibility and enhancing model generalization.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A4.SS0.SSS0.Px1.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A4.SS0.SSS0.Px1.p2.1" data-translate-id="chunk-280">At the execution level, our RL framework treats every agent task as an independent asynchronous coroutine. Each task can recursively trigger sub-task rollouts, simplifying the implementation of complex multi-agent paradigms such as <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A4.SS0.SSS0.Px1.p2.1.1">Parallel-Agent RL</span> and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A4.SS0.SSS0.Px1.p2.1.2">Agent-as-Judge</span>. As shown in the figure <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#A4.F10" title="Figure 10 ‣ Appendix D Unified Agentic Reinforcement Learning Environment ‣ Kimi K2.5: Visual Agentic Intelligence"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">10</span></a>, a dedicated <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="A4.SS0.SSS0.Px1.p2.1.3">Rollout Manager</span> orchestrates up to 100,000 concurrent agent tasks during the RL process, providing fine-grained control to enable features like partial rollout <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#bib.bib107" title="Kimi k1. 5: scaling reinforcement learning with llms">30</a>]</cite>. Upon activation, each task acquires an environment instance from a managed pool, equipped with a sandbox and specialized tools.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A4.SS0.SSS0.Px2">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-281">Inference Engine Co-design</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A4.SS0.SSS0.Px2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A4.SS0.SSS0.Px2.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-282">Our framework strictly follows a <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A4.SS0.SSS0.Px2.p1.1.1">Token-in-Token-out</span> paradigm. We also record log probabilities for all inference engine outputs to perform train-inference mismatch correction, ensuring stable RL training. A co-design of inference engine for RL requirements has allowed us to support these features by custom inference APIs for RL.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A4.SS0.SSS0.Px2.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A4.SS0.SSS0.Px2.p2.1" data-translate-id="chunk-283">Besides a comprehensive suite of built-in white-box environments, there are also black-box environments that can only run under standard LLM API protocol, missing the opportunity to use advanced features offered by our custom API protocol. To facilitate model optimization under black-box environments,
we developed <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A4.SS0.SSS0.Px2.p2.1.1">LLM Gateway</span>, which is a proxy service that keeps detailed records of rollout requests and responses under our custom protocol.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A4.SS0.SSS0.Px3">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-284">Monitoring and debugging</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A4.SS0.SSS0.Px3.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A4.SS0.SSS0.Px3.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-285">It is a challenging task to optimize performance of a highly-parallel asynchronous execution system, while ensuring correctness. We develop a series of tools for performance monitoring, profiling, data visualization and data verification. We found these to be instrumental in debugging and ensuring both the efficiency and correctness of our Agentic RL.</p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section class="ltx_appendix" id="A5">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_appendix" data-translate-id="chunk-286">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_appendix">Appendix E </span>Evaluation Settings</h2>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-287">This section provides comprehensive configuration details and testing protocols for all benchmarks reported in Table&nbsp;<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#S5.T4" title="Table 4 ‣ Benchmarks ‣ 5.1.1 Evaluation Settings ‣ 5.1 Main Results ‣ 5 Evaluations ‣ Kimi K2.5: Visual Agentic Intelligence"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">4</span></a>.</p>
</div>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="A5.SS1">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection" data-translate-id="chunk-288">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">E.1 </span>General Evaluation Protocol</h3>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS1.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-289">Unless explicitly stated otherwise, all experiments for Kimi-K2.5 adhere to the following hyperparameter configuration:</p>
<ul class="ltx_itemize" id="A5.I1">
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I1.i1" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A5.I1.i1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I1.i1.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-290"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.I1.i1.p1.1.1">Temperature:</span> <math alttext="1.0" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A5.I1.i1.p1.1.m1" intent=":literal"><semantics><mn>1.0</mn><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1.0</annotation></semantics></math></p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I1.i2" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A5.I1.i2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I1.i2.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-291"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.I1.i2.p1.1.1">Top-p:</span> <math alttext="0.95" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A5.I1.i2.p1.1.m1" intent=":literal"><semantics><mn>0.95</mn><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">0.95</annotation></semantics></math></p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I1.i3" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A5.I1.i3.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I1.i3.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-292"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.I1.i3.p1.1.1">Context Length:</span> <math alttext="256\text{k}" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A5.I1.i3.p1.1.m1" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mn>256</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mtext>k</mtext></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">256\text{k}</annotation></semantics></math> tokens</p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="A5.SS2">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection" data-translate-id="chunk-293">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">E.2 </span>Baselines</h3>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS2.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-294">For baseline models, we report results under their respective high-performance reasoning configurations:</p>
<ul class="ltx_itemize" id="A5.I2">
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I2.i1" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A5.I2.i1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I2.i1.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-295"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.I2.i1.p1.1.1">Claude Opus 4.5:</span> Extended thinking mode</p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I2.i2" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A5.I2.i2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I2.i2.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-296"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.I2.i2.p1.1.1">GPT-5.2:</span> Maximum reasoning effort (<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="A5.I2.i2.p1.1.2">xhigh</span>)</p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I2.i3" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A5.I2.i3.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I2.i3.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-297"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.I2.i3.p1.1.1">Gemini 3 Pro:</span> High thinking level</p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I2.i4" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A5.I2.i4.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I2.i4.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-298"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.I2.i4.p1.1.1">DeepSeek-V3.2:</span> Thinking mode enabled (for text-only benchmarks)</p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I2.i5" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A5.I2.i5.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I2.i5.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-299"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.I2.i5.p1.1.1">Qwen3-VL-235B-A22B:</span> Thinking mode (for vision benchmarks only)</p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS2.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS2.p2.1" data-translate-id="chunk-300">For vision and multimodal benchmarks, GPT-5.2-xhigh exhibited an approximate 10% failure rate (i.e., no output generated despite three retry attempts) during vision evaluations. These failures were treated as incorrect predictions, meaning that the reported scores may be conservative lower bounds of the model’s true capability.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS2.p3">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS2.p3.1" data-translate-id="chunk-301">In addition, because we were unable to consistently access a stable GPT-5.2 API, we skipped some benchmarks with high evaluation costs, such as WideSearch.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="A5.SS3">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection" data-translate-id="chunk-302">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">E.3 </span>Text Benchmarks</h3>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A5.SS3.SSS0.Px1">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-303">Reasoning Benchmarks.</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS3.SSS0.Px1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS3.SSS0.Px1.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-304">For high-complexity reasoning benchmarks, including HLE-Full, AIME 2025, HMMT 2025, GPQA-Diamond, and IMO-AnswerBench, we enforce a maximum completion budget of <math alttext="96\text{k}" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A5.SS3.SSS0.Px1.p1.1.m1" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mn>96</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mtext>k</mtext></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">96\text{k}</annotation></semantics></math> tokens to ensure sufficient reasoning depth. To reduce variance arising from stochastic reasoning paths, results on AIME 2025 and HMMT 2025 (Feb) are averaged over 64 independent runs (Avg@64), while GPQA-Diamond is averaged over 8 runs (Avg@8).</p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A5.SS3.SSS0.Px2">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-305">LongBench v2.</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS3.SSS0.Px2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS3.SSS0.Px2.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-306">For a fair comparison, we standardize all input contexts to approximately <math alttext="128\text{k}" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A5.SS3.SSS0.Px2.p1.1.m1" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mn>128</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mtext>k</mtext></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">128\text{k}</annotation></semantics></math> tokens using the same truncation strategy as in&nbsp;<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#bib.bib34" title="LongBench v2: towards deeper understanding and reasoning on realistic long-context multitasks">8</a>]</cite>.
We observe that GPT5.2-xhigh frequently produces free-form question–answer style responses rather than the required multiple-choice format.
Therefore, we report results using GPT5.2-high, which consistently adheres to the expected output format.</p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="A5.SS4">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection" data-translate-id="chunk-307">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">E.4 </span>Image and Video Benchmarks</h3>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS4.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS4.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-308">All image and video understanding evaluations utilize the following configuration:</p>
<ul class="ltx_itemize" id="A5.I3">
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I3.i1" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A5.I3.i1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I3.i1.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-309"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.I3.i1.p1.1.1">Maximum Tokens:</span> <math alttext="64\text{k}" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A5.I3.i1.p1.1.m1" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mn>64</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mtext>k</mtext></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">64\text{k}</annotation></semantics></math></p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I3.i2" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A5.I3.i2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I3.i2.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-310"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.I3.i2.p1.1.1">Sampling:</span> Averaged over 3 independent runs (Avg@3)</p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A5.SS4.SSS0.Px1">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-311">ZeroBench (w/ tools).</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS4.SSS0.Px1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS4.SSS0.Px1.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-312">Multi-step reasoning evaluations use constrained step-wise generation:</p>
<ul class="ltx_itemize" id="A5.I4">
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I4.i1" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A5.I4.i1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I4.i1.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-313"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.I4.i1.p1.1.1">Max Tokens per Step:</span> <math alttext="24\text{k}" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A5.I4.i1.p1.1.m1" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mn>24</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">​</mo><mtext>k</mtext></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">24\text{k}</annotation></semantics></math></p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I4.i2" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A5.I4.i2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I4.i2.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-314"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.I4.i2.p1.1.1">Maximum Steps:</span> <math alttext="30" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A5.I4.i2.p1.1.m1" intent=":literal"><semantics><mn>30</mn><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">30</annotation></semantics></math></p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A5.SS4.SSS0.Px2">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-315">MMMU-Pro.</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS4.SSS0.Px2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS4.SSS0.Px2.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-316">We adhere strictly to the official evaluation protocol: input order is preserved for all modalities, with images prepended to text sequences as specified in the benchmark guidelines.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A5.SS4.SSS0.Px3">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-317">Sampling Strategies for Video Benchmarks.</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS4.SSS0.Px3.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS4.SSS0.Px3.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-318">For short video benchmarks (VideoMMMU, MMVU &amp; MotionBench), we sample 128 uniform input frames with a maximum spatial resolution at 896; 2048 uniform frames are sampled for long video benchmarks (Video-MME, LongVideoBench &amp; LVBench) with 448 spatial resolution.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A5.SS4.SSS0.Px4">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-319">Specialized Metrics.</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS4.SSS0.Px4.p1">
<ul class="ltx_itemize" id="A5.I5">
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I5.i1" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A5.I5.i1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I5.i1.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-320"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.I5.i1.p1.1.1">OmniDocBench 1.5:</span> Scores are computed as <math alttext="(1-\text{normalized Levenshtein distance})\times 100" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A5.I5.i1.p1.1.m1" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mtext>normalized Levenshtein distance</mtext></mrow><mo rspace="0.055em" stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mn>100</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(1-\text{normalized Levenshtein distance})\times 100</annotation></semantics></math>, where higher values indicate superior OCR and document understanding accuracy.</p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I5.i2" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A5.I5.i2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I5.i2.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-321"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.I5.i2.p1.1.1">WorldVQA:</span> Access available at <a class="ltx_ref ltx_url ltx_font_typewriter" href="https://github.com/MoonshotAI/WorldVQA" title="">https://github.com/MoonshotAI/WorldVQA</a>. This benchmark evaluates atomic, vision-centric world knowledge requiring fine-grained visual recognition and geographic understanding.</p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="A5.SS5">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection" data-translate-id="chunk-322">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">E.5 </span>Coding and Software Engineering</h3>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px1">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-323">Terminal Bench 2.0.</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px1.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-324">All scores are obtained using the default Terminus-2 agent framework with the provided JSON parser. Notably, we evaluate under <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px1.p1.1.1">non-thinking mode</span> because our current context management implementation for thinking mode is technically incompatible with Terminus-2’s conversation state handling.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px2">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-325">SWE-Bench Series.</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px2.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-326">We employ an internally developed evaluation framework featuring a minimal tool set: <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px2.p1.1.1">bash</span>, <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px2.p1.1.2">create_file</span>, <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px2.p1.1.3">insert</span>, <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px2.p1.1.4">view</span>, <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px2.p1.1.5">str_replace</span>, and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px2.p1.1.6">submit</span>. System prompts are specifically tailored for repository-level code manipulation. Peak performance is achieved under <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px2.p1.1.7">non-thinking mode</span> across all SWE-Bench variants (Verified, Multilingual, and Pro).</p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px3">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-327">CyberGym.</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px3.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px3.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-328">Claude Opus 4.5 results for this benchmark are reported under non-thinking settings as specified in their technical documentation. We report scores in the difficulty level 1 (the primary setting).</p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px4">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-329">PaperBench.</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px4.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px4.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-330">We report the scores under the CodeDev setting.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px5">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-331">Sampling.</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px5.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS5.SSS0.Px5.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-332">All coding task results are averaged over 5 independent runs (Avg@5) to ensure stability across environment initialization and non-deterministic test case ordering.</p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="A5.SS6">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection" data-translate-id="chunk-333">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">E.6 </span>Agentic Evaluation</h3>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A5.SS6.SSS0.Px1">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-334">Tool Setting.</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS6.SSS0.Px1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS6.SSS0.Px1.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-335">Kimi-K2.5 is equipped with web search tool, code interpreter (Python execution environment), and web browsing tools for all agentic evaluations, including HLE with tools and agentic search benchmarks (BrowseComp, WideSearch, DeepSearchQA, FinSearchComp T2&amp;T3 and Seal-0).</p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A5.SS6.SSS0.Px2">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-336">Context Management Strategies.</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS6.SSS0.Px2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS6.SSS0.Px2.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-337">To handle the extended trajectory lengths inherent in complex agentic tasks, we implement domain-specific context management protocols. Unless otherwise specified below, <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.SS6.SSS0.Px2.p1.1.1">no context management</span> is applied to agentic evaluations; tasks exceeding the model’s supported context window are directly counted as failures rather than truncated.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS6.SSS0.Px2.p2">
<ul class="ltx_itemize" id="A5.I6">
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I6.i1" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.I6.i1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I6.i1.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-338"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.I6.i1.p1.1.1">Humanity’s Last Exam (HLE).</span> For the HLE tool-augmented setting, we employ a <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A5.I6.i1.p1.1.2">Hide-Tool-Result Context Management</span> strategy: when the context length exceeds predefined thresholds, only the most recent round of tool messages (observations and return values) is retained, while the reasoning chain and thinking processes from all previous steps are preserved in full.</p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I6.i2" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A5.I6.i2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I6.i2.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-339"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.I6.i2.p1.1.1">BrowseComp.</span> For BrowseComp evaluations, our evaluation contains both with and without context management settings. Under the context management setting, we adopt the same <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A5.I6.i2.p1.1.2">discard-all</span> strategy proposed by DeepSeek, where all history is truncated once token thresholds are exceeded.</p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A5.SS6.SSS0.Px3">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-340">System Prompt.</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS6.SSS0.Px3.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS6.SSS0.Px3.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-341">All agentic search and HLE evaluations utilize the following unified system prompt, where <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="A5.SS6.SSS0.Px3.p1.1.1">DATE</span> is dynamically set to the current timestamp:</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS6.SSS0.Px3.p2">
<pre class="ltx_verbatim ltx_font_typewriter" id="A5.SS6.SSS0.Px3.p2.1">You are Kimi, today’s date: DATE.
Your task is to help the user with their questions by using various tools,
thinking deeply, and ultimately answering the user’s questions.

Please follow the following principles strictly during the deep research:
1. Always focus on the user’s original question during the research process,
   avoiding deviating from the topic.
2. When facing uncertain information, use search tools to confirm.
3. When searching, filter high-trust sources (such as authoritative websites,
   academic databases, and professional media) and maintain a critical mindset
   towards low-trust sources.
4. When performing numerical calculations, prioritize using programming tools
   to ensure accuracy.
5. Please use the format [^index^] to cite any information you use.
6. This is a **Very Difficult** problemdo not underestimate it. You must use
   tools to help your reasoning and then solve the problem.
7. Before you finally give your answer, please recall what the question is
   asking for.
</pre>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A5.SS6.SSS0.Px4">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-342">Sampling Protocol.</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS6.SSS0.Px4.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS6.SSS0.Px4.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-343">To account for the inherent stochasticity in search engine result rankings and dynamic web content availability, results for Seal-0 and WideSearch are averaged over 4 independent runs (Avg@4). All other agentic benchmarks are evaluated under single-run protocols unless explicitly stated otherwise.</p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="A5.SS7">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection" data-translate-id="chunk-344">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">E.7 </span>Computer-Use Evaluation</h3>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A5.SS7.SSS0.Px1">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-345">Hyperparameter Settings.</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS7.SSS0.Px1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS7.SSS0.Px1.p1.5" data-translate-id="chunk-346">We set <math alttext="\texttt{max\_steps\_per\_episode}=100" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A5.SS7.SSS0.Px1.p1.1.m1" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mtext class="ltx_mathvariant_monospace">max_steps_per_episode</mtext><mo>=</mo><mn>100</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\texttt{max\_steps\_per\_episode}=100</annotation></semantics></math> for all experiments, with <math alttext="\texttt{temperature}=0" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A5.SS7.SSS0.Px1.p1.2.m2" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mtext class="ltx_mathvariant_monospace">temperature</mtext><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\texttt{temperature}=0</annotation></semantics></math> for OSWorld-Verified and <math alttext="\texttt{temperature}=0.1" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A5.SS7.SSS0.Px1.p1.3.m3" intent=":literal"><semantics><mrow><mtext class="ltx_mathvariant_monospace">temperature</mtext><mo>=</mo><mn>0.1</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\texttt{temperature}=0.1</annotation></semantics></math> for WebArena. Due to resource constraints, all models are evaluated in a one-shot setting. Adhering to the OpenCUA configuration&nbsp;<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#bib.bib6" title="OpenCUA: open foundations for computer-use agents">63</a>]</cite>, the agent context includes the last 3 history images, the complete thought history, and the task instruction. For WebArena, we manually corrected errors in the evaluation scripts and employed <span class="ltx_text ltx_markedasmath ltx_font_typewriter" id="A5.SS7.SSS0.Px1.p1.5.1">GPT-4o</span> as the judge model for the <span class="ltx_text ltx_markedasmath ltx_font_typewriter" id="A5.SS7.SSS0.Px1.p1.5.2">fuzzy_match</span> function. To ensure fair comparison, Claude Opus 4.5 is evaluated solely with computer-use tools (excluding browser tools), a departure from the System Card configuration&nbsp;<cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#bib.bib226" title="Claude opus 4.5 system card">4</a>]</cite>.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A5.SS7.SSS0.Px2">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-347">System Prompt</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS7.SSS0.Px2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS7.SSS0.Px2.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-348">We utilize a unified system prompt for all computer use tasks:</p>
<pre class="ltx_verbatim ltx_font_typewriter" id="A5.SS7.SSS0.Px2.p1.2">You are a GUI agent. You are given an instruction, a screenshot of the screen and your
previous interactions with the computer. You need to perform a series of actions to
complete the task. The password of the computer is {password}.

For each step, provide your response in this format:
{thought}
## Action:
{action}
## Code:
{code}

In the code section, the code should be either pyautogui code or one of the following
functions wrapped in the code block:
- {"name": "computer.wait", "description": "Make the computer wait for 20 seconds
for installation, running code, etc.", "parameters": {"type": "object", "properties":
{}, "required": []}}
- {"name": "computer.terminate", "description": "Terminate the current task and report
its completion status", "parameters": {"type": "object", "properties": {"status":
{"type": "string", "enum": ["success", "failure"], "description": "The status of the
task"}, "answer": {"type": "string", "description": "The answer of the task"}},
"required": ["status"]}}
</pre>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="A5.SS8">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection" data-translate-id="chunk-349">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">E.8 </span>Agent Swarm Configuration</h3>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A5.SS8.SSS0.Px1">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-350">Tool Setting.</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS8.SSS0.Px1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS8.SSS0.Px1.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-351">In addition to the core toolset described in Appendix&nbsp;<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#A5.SS6" title="E.6 Agentic Evaluation ‣ Appendix E Evaluation Settings ‣ Kimi K2.5: Visual Agentic Intelligence"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">E.6</span></a> (web search, code interpreter, and web browsing), the orchestrator is equipped with two specialized tools for sub-agent creation and scheduling:</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS8.SSS0.Px1.p2">
<ul class="ltx_itemize" id="A5.I7">
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I7.i1" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A5.I7.i1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I7.i1.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-352"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="A5.I7.i1.p1.1.1">create_subagent</span>: Instantiates a specialized sub-agent with a custom system prompt and identifier for reuse across tasks.</p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I7.i2" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A5.I7.i2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I7.i2.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-353"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="A5.I7.i2.p1.1.1">assign_task</span>: Dispatches assignments to created sub-agents.</p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS8.SSS0.Px1.p3">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS8.SSS0.Px1.p3.1" data-translate-id="chunk-354">The tool schemas are provided below:</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS8.SSS0.Px1.p4">
<pre class="ltx_verbatim ltx_font_typewriter" id="A5.SS8.SSS0.Px1.p4.1">{
 "name": "create_subagent",
 "description": "Create a custom subagent with specific system prompt
   and name for reuse.",
 "parameters": {
   "type": "object",
   "properties": {
     "name": {
       "type": "string",
       "description": "Unique name for this agent configuration"
     },
     "system_prompt": {
       "type": "string",
       "description": "System prompt defining the agent’s role,
         capabilities, and boundaries"
     }
   },
   "required": ["name", "system_prompt"]
 }
}
{
 "name": "assign_task",
 "description": "Launch a new agent.\nUsage notes:\n
   1. You can launch multiple agents concurrently whenever possible,
      to maximize performance;\n
   2. When the agent is done, it will return a single message back to you.",
 "parameters": {
   "type": "object",
   "properties": {
     "agent": {
       "type": "string",
       "description": "Specify which created agent to use."
     },
     "prompt": {
       "type": "string",
       "description": "The task for the agent to perform"
     }
   },
   "required": ["agent", "prompt"]
 }
}
</pre>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A5.SS8.SSS0.Px2">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-355">Step Limits.</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS8.SSS0.Px2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.SS8.SSS0.Px2.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-356">When operating in Agent Swarm mode, we set computational budgets for the orchestrator and sub-agents. Step limits apply to the aggregate count of tool invocations and environment interactions.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS8.SSS0.Px2.p2">
<ul class="ltx_itemize" id="A5.I8">
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I8.i1" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A5.I8.i1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I8.i1.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-357"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.I8.i1.p1.1.1">BrowseComp:</span> The orchestrator is constrained to a maximum of 15 steps. Each spawned sub-agent operates under a limit of 100 steps (i.e., up to 100 tool calls per sub-agent).</p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I8.i2" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A5.I8.i2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I8.i2.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-358"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.I8.i2.p1.1.1">WideSearch:</span> Both the orchestrator and each sub-agent are allocated a maximum budget of 100 steps.</p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="A5.I8.i3" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A5.I8.i3.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A5.I8.i3.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-359"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A5.I8.i3.p1.1.1">In-house Bench:</span> The orchestrator is constrained to a maximum of 100 steps. Each spawned sub-agent operates under a limit of 50 steps .</p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_paragraph" id="A5.SS8.SSS0.Px3">
<h5 class="ltx_title ltx_title_paragraph" data-translate-id="chunk-360">System Prompt.</h5>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A5.SS8.SSS0.Px3.p1">
<pre class="ltx_verbatim ltx_font_typewriter" id="A5.SS8.SSS0.Px3.p1.1">You are Kimi, a professional and meticulous expert in information collection and organization.
You fully understand user needs, skillfully use various tools, and complete tasks with the
highest efficiency.
# Task Description
After receiving users’ questions, you need to fully understand their needs and think
about and plan how to complete the tasks efficiently and quickly.
# Available Tools
To help you complete tasks better and faster, I have provided you with the following tools:
1. Search tool: You can use the search engine to retrieve information, supporting multiple
queries in parallel.
2. Browser tools: You can visit web links (web pages, PDFs, etc.), get page content, and
perform interactions such as clicking, inputting, finding, and scrolling.
3. Sub Agent tools:
   - ‘create_subagent‘: Create a new sub-agent with a unique name and clear, specific
   system prompt.
   - ‘assign_task‘: Delegate tasks to created sub-agents. Sub-agents can also use search
   and browser tools.
4. Other tools: Including code execution (IPython, Shell).
</pre>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="A5.SS9">

<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">E.9 </span>GDPVal</h3>

<section class="ltx_appendix" id="A6">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_appendix" data-translate-id="chunk-365">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_appendix">Appendix F </span>Visualization</h2>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A6.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A6.p1.1" data-translate-id="chunk-366">Figure&nbsp;<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#A5.F11" title="Figure 11 ‣ E.9 GDPVal ‣ Appendix E Evaluation Settings ‣ Kimi K2.5: Visual Agentic Intelligence"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">11</span></a> demonstrates our Agent Swarm tackling a challenging long-form video understanding task: analyzing a complete playthrough of <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A6.p1.1.1">Black Myth: Wukong</span> (24 hours of continuous gameplay across 32 videos, totaling 40GB). The system employs a hierarchical multi-agent architecture where a Main Agent orchestrates parallel Sub Agents to process individual video segments independently. Each sub agent performs frame extraction, temporal event analysis, and key moment identification (e.g., boss fights, level-ups). The Main Agent subsequently aggregates these distributed analyses to synthesize a comprehensive HTML showcase featuring chronological timelines, embedded video clips, and interactive visualizations. This example demonstrates the system’s ability to handle massive-scale multimodal content through parallelization while maintaining coherent long-context understanding.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A6.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A6.p2.1" data-translate-id="chunk-367">Figure&nbsp;<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2602.02276v1#A5.F12" title="Figure 12 ‣ E.9 GDPVal ‣ Appendix E Evaluation Settings ‣ Kimi K2.5: Visual Agentic Intelligence"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">12</span></a> presents qualitative examples of Kimi K2.5 solving diverse visual reasoning tasks via tool-augmented reasoning. The model demonstrates: <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A6.p2.1.1">(1)</span> Maze Solving—processing binary image segmentation and implementing pathfinding algorithms (BFS) to navigate complex mazes; <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A6.p2.1.2">(2)</span> Pie Chart Analysis—performing pixel-level color segmentation and geometric calculations to determine precise area proportions; and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A6.p2.1.3">(3)</span> Spot-the-Difference—employing computer vision techniques to detect pixel-level discrepancies between image pairs. These examples highlight the model’s capability to decompose complex visual problems into executable code, iteratively refine strategies based on intermediate results, and synthesize precise answers through quantitative visual analysis.</p>
</div>
</section>
